Wikipedia summary¶

This is the text summarization of wikipedia article.

  1. In wikipedia , there are millions of articles are present
  2. length of each article ~ more than 10000 worlds
  3. so it is difficult to read whole article, so we will summarize article & provide most important sentences whic gives impact pf article

so lets get started

there are numbers of way we can do text summarization, we will look into some of the technique

  1. sumy library
  2. by python coding
  3. gensim summarizer

Lets get started with sumy python library

import sumy library and from sumy import LsaSummarizer,LuhnSummarizer,EdmundsonSummarizer,LexRankSummarize these are various algorithm available which use for text summarization

you can find more info about sumy https://pypi.org/project/sumy/

Gensim summarizer

we can do summarization using gensim API summarize https://radimrehurek.com/gensim/summarization/summariser.html

And we can only use python to do text summarization

Lets get started

In [68]:
#import libraries

#Analysis
import pandas as pd

#Natural language processing
import nltk

#reguler expression
import re

#web scraping
import bs4 as bs

import requests
import heapq
  1. we will url wiki page https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_war which contain information about world war
  2. with request.get we will handle the request
  3. with beautiful soap library , we will exctract contain from web page and with pretiffy() , will display the web contain
  4. now, data is in raw form. it contain all html tag present in the web page which is not usefull for us.
  5. next step is now data cleaning
In [69]:
sourse=requests.get('https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_war')
su=sourse.content
In [70]:
soup = bs.BeautifulSoup(su,'html.parser')
In [71]:
soup.prettify()

style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n          <div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0">\n           <div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left">\n            <a href="/wiki/Category:Military_lists" title="Category:Military lists">\n             Lists\n            </a>\n               Writers\n              </a>\n             </li>\n            </ul>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n        <tr>\n         <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">\n          <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n           <ul>\n            <li class="nv-view">\n             <a href="/wiki/Template:War" title="Template:War">\n              <abbr title="View this template">\n               v\n              </abbr>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="nv-talk">\n             <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:War" title="Template talk:War">\n              <abbr title="Discuss this template">\n               t\n              </abbr>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="nv-edit">\n             <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:War&amp;action=edit">\n              <abbr title="Edit this template">\n               e\n              </abbr>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </div>\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n       </tbody>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        world war\n       </b>\n       is a large-scale\n       <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">\n        war\n       </a>\n       which affects the whole world directly or indirectly. World wars span multiple countries on multiple\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continents" title="Continents">\n        continents\n       </a>\n       or just two countries, with battles fought in many\n       <a href="/wiki/Theater_(warfare)" title="Theater (warfare)">\n        theaters\n       </a>\n       . While a variety of global conflicts have been subjectively deemed "world wars", such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">\n        Cold War\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">\n        War on Terror\n       </a>\n       , the term is widely and usually accepted only as it is retrospectively applied to two major international conflicts that occurred during the 20th century:\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">\n        World War I\n       </a>\n       (191418) and\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       (193945).\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/>\n       <div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n        <span class="toctogglespan">\n         <label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox">\n         </label>\n        </span>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Origin_of_the_term">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Origin of the term\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2">\n         <a href="#First_World_War">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           First World War\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3">\n         <a href="#Second_World_War">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Second World War\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4">\n         <a href="#Third_World_War">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Third World War\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5">\n         <a href="#Other_global_conflicts">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Other global conflicts\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6">\n           <a href="#Wars_with_higher_death_tolls_than_the_First_World_War">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Wars with higher death tolls than the First World War\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#Wars_spanning_continents">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Wars spanning continents\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_term">\n        Origin of the term\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_war&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origin of the term">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">\n         Oxford English Dictionary\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       cited the first known usage in the\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English language\n       </a>\n       to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">\n        Scottish\n       </a>\n       newspaper,\n       <i>\n        The People\'s Journal\n       </i>\n       , in 1848: "A war among the great powers is now necessarily a world-war." The term "world war" is used by\n       <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">\n        Karl Marx\n       </a>\n       and his associate,\n       <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">\n        Friedrich Engels\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in a series of articles published around 1850 called\n       <i>\n        The Class Struggles in France\n       </i>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Rasmus_B._Anderson" title="Rasmus B. Anderson">\n        Rasmus B. Anderson\n       </a>\n       in 1889 described an episode in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teutonic_mythology" title="Teutonic mythology">\n        Teutonic mythology\n       </a>\n       as a world war (Swedish:\n       <i>\n        vrldskrig\n       </i>\n       ), justifying this description by a line in an\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">\n        Old Norse\n       </a>\n       epic poem, "\n       <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lusp%C3%A1" title="Vlusp">\n        Vlusp\n       </a>\n       : folcvig fyrst i heimi" ("The first great war in the world".)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       German writer August Wilhelm Otto Niemann had used the term "world war" in the title of his anti-British novel,\n       <i>\n        Der Weltkrieg: Deutsche Trume\n       </i>\n       (\n       <i>\n        The World War: German Dreams\n       </i>\n       ) in 1904, published in English as\n       <i>\n        The Coming Conquest of England\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In English, the term "First World War" had been used by\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_%C3%A0_Court_Repington" title="Charles  Court Repington">\n        Charles  Court Repington\n       </a>\n       , as a title for his memoirs (published in 1920); he had noted his discussion on the matter with a Major Johnstone of\n       <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">\n        Harvard University\n       </a>\n       in his diary entry of September 10, 1918.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The term "World War I" was coined by\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">\n         Time\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       magazine on page 28b of its June 12, 1939 issue. In the same article, on page 32, the term "World War II" was first used speculatively to describe the upcoming war. The first use for the actual war came in its issue of September 11, 1939.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One week earlier, on September 4, the day after France and the United Kingdom declared war on Germany, the Danish newspaper\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Kristeligt_Dagblad" title="Kristeligt Dagblad">\n         Kristeligt Dagblad\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       used the term on its front page, saying "The Second World War broke out yesterday at 11 a.m."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Speculative_fiction" title="Speculative fiction">\n        Speculative fiction\n       </a>\n       authors had been noting the concept of a Second World War in 1919 and 1920, when\n       <a href="/wiki/Milo_Hastings" title="Milo Hastings">\n        Milo Hastings\n       </a>\n       wrote his\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dystopian" title="Dystopian">\n        dystopian\n       </a>\n       novel,\n       <i>\n        City of Endless Night\n       </i>\n       .\nOther languages have also adopted the "world war" terminology, for example; in\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       : "world war" is translated as\n       <i>\n        guerre mondiale\n       </i>\n       , in\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">\n        German\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n        Weltkrieg\n       </i>\n       (which, prior to the war, had been used in the more abstract meaning of a global conflict), in\n       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">\n        Italian\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n        guerra mondiale\n       </i>\n       , in\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n        guerra mundial\n       </i>\n       , in\n       <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">\n        Danish\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">\n        Norwegian\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n        verdenskrig\n       </i>\n       , and in\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n         \n       </i>\n       (\n       <i>\n        mirovaya voyna\n       </i>\n       .)\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War">\n        First World War\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_war&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: First World War">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">\n        World War I\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       World War I occurred from 1914 to 1918. In terms of human\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_technology" title="History of technology">\n        technological history\n       </a>\n       , the scale of World War I was enabled by the technological advances of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_industrial_revolution" title="Second industrial revolution">\n        second industrial revolution\n       </a>\n       and the resulting\n       <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">\n        globalization\n       </a>\n       that allowed global power projection and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">\n        mass production\n       </a>\n       of military hardware. Wars on such a scale have not been repeated since the onset of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Age" title="Atomic Age">\n        Atomic Age\n       </a>\n       and the resulting danger of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mutually-assured_destruction" title="Mutually-assured destruction">\n        mutually-assured destruction\n       </a>\n       . It had been recognized that the complex system of opposing alliances (the\n       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">\n        German\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">\n        Austro-Hungarian\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">\n        Ottoman\n       </a>\n       Empires against the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">\n        British\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">\n        French\n       </a>\n       Empires) was likely to lead to a worldwide conflict if a war broke out. Due to this fact, a very minute conflict between two countries had the potential to set off a\n       <a href="/wiki/Domino_effect" title="Domino effect">\n        domino effect\n       </a>\n       of alliances, triggering a world war. The fact that the powers involved had large overseas empires virtually guaranteed that such a war would be worldwide, as the colonies\' resources would be a crucial strategic factor. The same strategic considerations also ensured that the combatants would strike at each other\'s colonies, thus spreading the wars far more widely than those of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">\n        pre-Columbian\n       </a>\n       times.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_crimes" title="War crimes">\n        War crimes\n       </a>\n       were perpetrated in World War I.\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons_in_World_War_I" title="Chemical weapons in World War I">\n        Chemical weapons\n       </a>\n       were used in the First World War despite the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hague_Conventions_of_1899_and_1907" title="Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907">\n        Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907\n       </a>\n       having outlawed the use of such weapons in warfare. The Ottoman Empire was responsible for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">\n        Armenian genocide\n       </a>\n       , the death of over one million Armenians during the First World War.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">\n        Second World War\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_war&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Second World War">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n       <tbody>\n        <tr>\n         <td class="mbox-image">\n          <div Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.\n            <br/>\n            <small>\n             <span class="plainlinks">\n              <i>\n               Find sources:\n              </i>\n class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22World+war%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">\n               JSTOR\n              </a>\n             </span>\n            </small>\n           </span>\n           <small class="date-container">\n            <i>\n             (\n             <span class="date">\n              September 2018\n             </span>\n             )\n            </i>\n           </small>\n           <small class="hide-when-compact">\n            <i>\n             (\n             <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n              Learn how and when to remove this template message\n             </a>\n             )\n            </i>\n           </small>\n          </div>\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n       </tbody>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The Second World War occurred from 1939 to 1945 and is the only conflict in which\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atomic_bombs" title="Atomic bombs">\n        atomic bombs\n       </a>\n       have been used.\n       <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">\n        Hiroshima\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">\n        Nagasaki\n       </a>\n       , in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Empire" title="Japanese Empire">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       , were\n       <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">\n        devastated\n       </a>\n       by atomic bombs dropped by the United States.\n       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">\n        Nazi Germany\n       </a>\n       was responsible for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genocides" title="Genocides">\n        genocides\n       </a>\n       , most notably\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">\n        the Holocaust\n       </a>\n       , the killing of six million\n       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">\n        Jews\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">\n        Soviet Union\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       deported and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interned" title="Interned">\n        interned\n       </a>\n       minority groups within their own borders, and largely because of the conflict, many ethnic\n       <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">\n        Germans\n       </a>\n       were later expelled from\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">\n        Eastern Europe\n       </a>\n       . Japan was responsible for attacking\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" title="Neutrality (international relations)">\n        neutral nations\n       </a>\n       without a\n       <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war" title="Declaration of war">\n        declaration of war\n       </a>\n       , such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">\n        bombing of Pearl Harbor\n       </a>\n       . It is also known for its brutal treatment and killing of Allied\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" title="Prisoners of war">\n        prisoners of war\n       </a>\n       and the inhabitants of\n       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">\n        Asia\n       </a>\n       . It also used Asians as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_labor" title="Forced labor">\n        forced laborers\n       </a>\n       and was responsible for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanking_massacre" title="Nanking massacre">\n        Nanking massacre\n       </a>\n       where 250,000 civilians in the city were brutally murdered by Japanese troops.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-combatants" title="Non-combatants">\n        Non-combatants\n       </a>\n       suffered at least as badly as or worse than\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combatants" title="Combatants">\n        combatants\n       </a>\n       , and the distinction between combatants and non-combatants was often blurred by belligerents of\n       <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">\n        total war\n       </a>\n       in both conflicts.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The outcome of World War II had a profound effect on the course of world history. The old European empires either collapsed or were dismantled as a direct result of the wars\' crushing costs and, in some cases, their fall was due to the defeat of imperial powers. The United States became firmly established as the dominant global superpower, along with its ideological foe, the Soviet Union, in close competition. The two superpowers exerted political influence over most of the world\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-states" title="Nation-states">\n        nation-states\n       </a>\n       for decades after the end of the Second World War. The modern international security, economic, and diplomatic system was created in the aftermath of the wars.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Institutions such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">\n        United Nations\n       </a>\n       were established to collectivize international affairs, with the explicit goal of preventing another outbreak of general war. The wars had also greatly changed the course of daily life. Technologies developed during wartime had a profound effect on peacetime life as well, such as by advances in\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">\n        jet aircraft\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Penicillin" title="Penicillin">\n        penicillin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">\n        nuclear energy\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_computers" title="Electronic computers">\n        electronic computers\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Third_World_War">\n        Third World War\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_war&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Third World War">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_III" title="World War III">\n        World War III\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">\n        atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki\n       </a>\n       during the Second World War, there has been a widespread and prolonged fear of a potential Third World War between nuclear-armed powers. The Third World War is generally considered a successor to the Second World War and is often suggested to become a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_war" title="Nuclear war">\n        nuclear war\n       </a>\n       , devastating in nature and likely much more violent than both the First and Second World Wars; in 1947,\n       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">\n        Albert Einstein\n       </a>\n       commented that "I know not with what weapons World War III will be fought, but World War IV will be fought with sticks and stones."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It has been anticipated and planned for by military and civil authorities and has been\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_III_in_popular_culture" title="World War III in popular culture">\n        explored in fiction\n       </a>\n       in many countries. Concepts have ranged from purely-conventional scenarios, to limited use of nuclear weapons, to the complete destruction of the planet\'s surface.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_global_conflicts">\n        Other global conflicts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_war&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Other global conflicts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">\n        Cold War\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">\n        War on Terror\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">\n        Second Congo War\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">\n        Syrian Civil War\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Civil_War_(2014%E2%80%932017)" title="Iraqi Civil War (20142017)">\n        Iraqi Civil War (20142017)\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_II" title="Cold War II">\n        Cold War II\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Various former government officials, politicians, authors, and military leaders (including the following people:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Woolsey" title="James Woolsey">\n        James Woolsey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WoolseyWWIV_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WoolseyWWIV-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_de_Marenches" title="Alexandre de Marenches">\n        Alexandre de Marenches\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarenchesWWIV_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MarenchesWWIV-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eliot_Cohen" title="Eliot Cohen">\n        Eliot Cohen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CohenWWIV_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CohenWWIV-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Subcomandante_Marcos" title="Subcomandante Marcos">\n        Subcomandante Marcos\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fourth_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fourth-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) have attempted to apply the labels of the "Third World War" and "Fourth World War" to various past and present global wars since the closing of the Second World War, for example, the Cold War and the War on Terror, respectively. Among these are former American, French, and Mexican government officials, military leaders, politicians, and authors. Despite their efforts, none of these wars are commonly deemed world wars.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Wars described by some historians as "World War Zero" include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years\' War">\n        Seven Years\' War\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the onset of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age_collapse" title="Late Bronze Age collapse">\n        Late Bronze Age collapse\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">\n        Second Congo War\n       </a>\n       (19982003) involved nine nations and led to ongoing low-level warfare despite an official peace and the first democratic elections in 2006. It has often been referred to as "Africa\'s World War".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the early-21st century the\n       <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">\n        Syrian Civil War\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Civil_War_(2014%E2%80%932017)" title="Iraqi Civil War (20142017)">\n        Iraqi Civil War\n       </a>\n       and their worldwide spillovers are sometimes described as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proxy_wars" title="Proxy wars">\n        proxy wars\n       </a>\n       waged between the United States and Russia,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turnproxy_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-turnproxy-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cain_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cain-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prox_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-prox-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stupid_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-stupid-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which led some commentators to characterize the situation as a "proto-world war" with nearly a dozen countries embroiled in two overlapping conflicts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-proto_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-proto-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wars_with_higher_death_tolls_than_the_First_World_War">\n        Wars with higher death tolls than the First World War\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_war&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Wars with higher death tolls than the First World War">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_wars_by_death_toll" title="List of wars by death toll">\n        List of wars by death toll\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I_casualties" title="World War I casualties">\n        World War I casualties\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The two world wars of the 20th century had caused unprecedented\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casualties" title="Casualties">\n        casualties\n       </a>\n       and destruction across the theaters of conflict.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There have been\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_wars_by_death_toll" title="List of wars by death toll">\n        several wars\n       </a>\n       that occurred with as many or more deaths than in the First World War (16,563,86840,000,000), including:\n      </p>\n      <table class="sortable wikitable" style="width:100%;">\n       <caption>\n        Estimated death tolls. text=""
for paragraph in soup.find_all('p'):
    text +=paragraph.text
print(text)

A world war is a large-scale war which affects the whole world directly or indirectly. World wars span multiple countries on multiple continents or just two countries, with battles fought in many theaters. While a variety of global conflicts have been subjectively deemed "world wars", such as the Cold War and the War on Terror, the term is widely and usually accepted only as it is retrospectively applied to two major international conflicts that occurred during the 20th century: World War I (191418) and World War II (193945).
The Oxford English Dictionary cited the first known usage in the English language to a Scottish newspaper, The People's Journal, in 1848: "A war among the great powers is now necessarily a world-war." The term "world war" is used by Karl Marx and his associate, Friedrich Engels,[1] in a series of articles published around 1850 called The Class Struggles in France. Rasmus B. Anderson in 1889 described an episode in Teutonic mythology as a world war (Swedish: vrldskrig), justifying this description by a line in an Old Norse epic poem, "Vlusp: folcvig fyrst i heimi" ("The first great war in the world".)[2] German writer August Wilhelm Otto Niemann had used the term "world war" in the title of his anti-British novel, Der Weltkrieg: Deutsche Trume (The World War: German Dreams) in 1904, published in English as The Coming Conquest of England.
In English, the term "First World War" had been used by Charles  Court Repington, as a title for his memoirs (published in 1920); he had noted his discussion on the matter with a Major Johnstone of Harvard University in his diary entry of September 10, 1918.[3]
The term "World War I" was coined by Time magazine on page 28b of its June 12, 1939 issue. In the same article, on page 32, the term "World War II" was first used speculatively to describe the upcoming war. The first use for the actual war came in its issue of September 11, 1939.[4] One week earlier, on September 4, the day after France and the United Kingdom declared war on Germany, the Danish newspaper Kristeligt Dagblad used the term on its front page, saying "The Second World War broke out yesterday at 11 a.m."[5]
Speculative fiction authors had been noting the concept of a Second World War in 1919 and 1920, when Milo Hastings wrote his dystopian novel, City of Endless Night.
Other languages have also adopted the "world war" terminology, for example; in French: "world war" is translated as guerre mondiale, in German: Weltkrieg (which, prior to the war, had been used in the more abstract meaning of a global conflict), in Italian: guerra mondiale, in Spanish and Portuguese: guerra mundial, in Danish and Norwegian: verdenskrig, and in Russian:   (mirovaya voyna.)
World War I occurred from 1914 to 1918. In terms of human technological history, the scale of World War I was enabled by the technological advances of the second industrial revolution and the resulting globalization that allowed global power projection and mass production of military hardware. Wars on such a scale have not been repeated since the onset of the Atomic Age and the resulting danger of mutually-assured destruction. It had been recognized that the complex system of opposing alliances (the German, Austro-Hungarian, and Ottoman Empires against the British, Russian, and French Empires) was likely to lead to a worldwide conflict if a war broke out. Due to this fact, a very minute conflict between two countries had the potential to set off a domino effect of alliances, triggering a world war. The fact that the powers involved had large overseas empires virtually guaranteed that such a war would be worldwide, as the colonies' resources would be a crucial strategic factor. The same strategic considerations also ensured that the combatants would strike at each other's colonies, thus spreading the wars far more widely than those of pre-Columbian times.
War crimes were perpetrated in World War I. Chemical weapons were used in the First World War despite the Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907 having outlawed the use of such weapons in warfare. The Ottoman Empire was responsible for the Armenian genocide, the death of over one million Armenians during the First World War.
The Second World War occurred from 1939 to 1945 and is the only conflict in which atomic bombs have been used. Hiroshima and Nagasaki, in Japan, were devastated by atomic bombs dropped by the United States. Nazi Germany was responsible for genocides, most notably the Holocaust, the killing of six million Jews. The United States, the Soviet Union, and Canada deported and interned minority groups within their own borders, and largely because of the conflict, many ethnic Germans were later expelled from Eastern Europe. Japan was responsible for attacking neutral nations without a declaration of war, such as the bombing of Pearl Harbor. It is also known for its brutal treatment and killing of Allied prisoners of war and the inhabitants of Asia. It also used Asians as forced laborers and was responsible for the Nanking massacre where 250,000 civilians in the city were brutally murdered by Japanese troops. Non-combatants suffered at least as badly as or worse than combatants, and the distinction between combatants and non-combatants was often blurred by belligerents of total war in both conflicts.[citation needed]
The outcome of World War II had a profound effect on the course of world history. The old European empires either collapsed or were dismantled as a direct result of the wars' crushing costs and, in some cases, their fall was due to the defeat of imperial powers. The United States became firmly established as the dominant global superpower, along with its ideological foe, the Soviet Union, in close competition. The two superpowers exerted political influence over most of the world's nation-states for decades after the end of the Second World War. The modern international security, economic, and diplomatic system was created in the aftermath of the wars.[citation needed]
Institutions such as the United Nations were established to collectivize international affairs, with the explicit goal of preventing another outbreak of general war. The wars had also greatly changed the course of daily life. Technologies developed during wartime had a profound effect on peacetime life as well, such as by advances in jet aircraft, penicillin, nuclear energy, and electronic computers.[citation needed]
Since the atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki during the Second World War, there has been a widespread and prolonged fear of a potential Third World War between nuclear-armed powers. The Third World War is generally considered a successor to the Second World War and is often suggested to become a nuclear war, devastating in nature and likely much more violent than both the First and Second World Wars; in 1947, Albert Einstein commented that "I know not with what weapons World War III will be fought, but World War IV will be fought with sticks and stones."[6][7] It has been anticipated and planned for by military and civil authorities and has been explored in fiction in many countries. Concepts have ranged from purely-conventional scenarios, to limited use of nuclear weapons, to the complete destruction of the planet's surface.
Various former government officials, politicians, authors, and military leaders (including the following people: James Woolsey,[8] Alexandre de Marenches,[9] Eliot Cohen,[10] and Subcomandante Marcos[11]) have attempted to apply the labels of the "Third World War" and "Fourth World War" to various past and present global wars since the closing of the Second World War, for example, the Cold War and the War on Terror, respectively. Among these are former American, French, and Mexican government officials, military leaders, politicians, and authors. Despite their efforts, none of these wars are commonly deemed world wars.
Wars described by some historians as "World War Zero" include the Seven Years' War[12] and the onset of the Late Bronze Age collapse.[13]
The Second Congo War (19982003) involved nine nations and led to ongoing low-level warfare despite an official peace and the first democratic elections in 2006. It has often been referred to as "Africa's World War".[14] During the early-21st century the Syrian Civil War and the Iraqi Civil War and their worldwide spillovers are sometimes described as proxy wars waged between the United States and Russia,[15][16][17][18] which led some commentators to characterize the situation as a "proto-world war" with nearly a dozen countries embroiled in two overlapping conflicts.[19]
The two world wars of the 20th century had caused unprecedented casualties and destruction across the theaters of conflict.[20] There have been several wars that occurred with as many or more deaths than in the First World War (16,563,86840,000,000), including:

There have been numerous wars spanning two or more continents throughout history, including:
  1. After exctracting the data from

    tag , we got useful data for summarization which we are looking for.

  2. Still the data is in noisy form it contain lot of stopwords , spaces, and other impurities which effects its weight.
  3. we will use python re library for data cleaning
In [73]:
#Preprocess data
text = re.sub(r'\[[0-9]*\]',' ',text)
text = re.sub(r'\s+',' ',text)
#text = re.sub(r'\[\]')
clean_text=text.lower()
clean_text = re.sub(r'\W',' ',clean_text)
clean_text=re.sub(r'[^\w]', ' ', clean_text)
clean_text=re.sub(r'[^\[a-z]]', ' ', clean_text)
clean_text = clean_text.replace("u'", " ")
clean_text = re.sub(r'\d',' ',clean_text)
clean_text = re.sub(r'\s+',' ',clean_text)
#clean_text=str(unicode(clean_text))
print(clean_text)

In [75]:
#stopword
stop_words = nltk.corpus.stopwords.words('english')
  1. for text summarization , we have to provide score for each sentences for that we have to provide score for each word present in sentence.
  2. we can give score to word using its number of occurance present in each sentence.
  3. below code will give dictionary for each word and its occorunce in each sentence
  4. from output its look like world & war word occurs many time
In [76]:
table={}
for data1 in nltk.word_tokenize(clean_text):
    if data1 not in stop_words:
        
        if data1 not in table.keys():
            table[data1] = 1
        else:
            table[data1] +=1
    

table

  1. after we get number of occurance for each word ,we can use it directly . we will divide each other word occurance with max word present in dataset which assign weight to each word
In [77]:
max_weight=max(table.values())

for weight in table.keys():
    table[weight]=table[weight]/max_weight

table

  1. now we will provide score to each sentence
  2. we will select only those sentence which has 25 or less word present in it, we can increase this limit but I guess it will also effect results , after taking different number I found 25 word for sentence will give pretty results
  3. to display top 10 sentece , we will use heapq library which sort the result and gives top 10 sentence
In [78]:
score_run={}
for sent in sentence:
        for word in nltk.word_tokenize(sent.lower()):
            
            if word in table.keys():
                
                if len(sent.split(' ')) < 25:
                    if sent not in score_run.keys():
                        score_run[sent] = table[word]
                    else:
                        score_run[sent] += table[word]
In [79]:
best_sentences = heapq.nlargest(10,score_run , key=score_run.get)

print('---------------------------------------------------------')
for sentence in best_sentences:
    print(sentence)

---------------------------------------------------------
A world war is a large-scale war which affects the whole world directly or indirectly.
In the same article, on page 32, the term "World War II" was first used speculatively to describe the upcoming war.
Wars described by some historians as "World War Zero" include the Seven Years' War and the onset of the Late Bronze Age collapse.
The two superpowers exerted political influence over most of the world's nation-states for decades after the end of the Second World War.
[citation needed] The outcome of World War II had a profound effect on the course of world history.
War crimes were perpetrated in World War I.
The Second World War occurred from 1939 to 1945 and is the only conflict in which atomic bombs have been used.
The Ottoman Empire was responsible for the Armenian genocide, the death of over one million Armenians during the First World War.
The term "World War I" was coined by Time magazine on page 28b of its June 12, 1939 issue.
It has often been referred to as "Africa's World War".

gensim summarizer¶

  1. we have discuss one technique for text summarization, now we will look into much simpler and easier technique calles gensim text summarizer
  2. import gensim.summarization API
  3. provide the text for which we want summy, in earlier we have sort and cleran the text and save in variable text
  4. with gensim we can do summarization using word count and ratio also, we will perfrom both the technique
  5. below is the summary for word_counbt=200 and for ratio=0.07
In [80]:
from gensim.summarization import summarize
import warnings

warnings.filterwarnings('ignore')
print('__________________________Summary with word count:_____________________________________')
url='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_war'
print (summarize(text, word_count=200))
print('-----------------------------summary with ratio------------------------------------------')
print (summarize(text, ratio=0.07))

__________________________Summary with word count:_____________________________________
One week earlier, on September 4, the day after France and the United Kingdom declared war on Germany, the Danish newspaper Kristeligt Dagblad used the term on its front page, saying "The Second World War broke out yesterday at 11 a.m." Speculative fiction authors had been noting the concept of a Second World War in 1919 and 1920, when Milo Hastings wrote his dystopian novel, City of Endless Night.
In terms of human technological history, the scale of World War I was enabled by the technological advances of the second industrial revolution and the resulting globalization that allowed global power projection and mass production of military hardware.
The Ottoman Empire was responsible for the Armenian genocide, the death of over one million Armenians during the First World War. The Second World War occurred from 1939 to 1945 and is the only conflict in which atomic bombs have been used.
Technologies developed during wartime had a profound effect on peacetime life as well, such as by advances in jet aircraft, penicillin, nuclear energy, and electronic computers.[citation needed] Since the atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki during the Second World War, there has been a widespread and prolonged fear of a potential Third World War between nuclear-armed powers.
-----------------------------summary with ratio------------------------------------------

In terms of human technological history, the scale of World War I was enabled by the technological advances of the second industrial revolution and the resulting globalization that allowed global power projection and mass production of military hardware.
The Ottoman Empire was responsible for the Armenian genocide, the death of over one million Armenians during the First World War. The Second World War occurred from 1939 to 1945 and is the only conflict in which atomic bombs have been used.

Sumy library¶

Sumy is python library which mostly used for text summarization, it has various types of API used for summarization we will look into 1 2 such API for text summarization LSAtextsummarizer and textranksummarizer

let's import the sumy library and require summarizer API which we are using for summarization

In [81]:
# Sumy Library for summarization

import sumy
from sumy.parsers.html import HtmlParser
from sumy.parsers.plaintext import PlaintextParser
from sumy.nlp.tokenizers import Tokenizer
from sumy.summarizers.lsa import LsaSummarizer
from sumy.nlp.stemmers import Stemmer
from sumy.utils import get_stop_words
 
from sumy.summarizers.luhn import LuhnSummarizer
from sumy.summarizers.edmundson import EdmundsonSummarizer
from sumy.summarizers.lex_rank import LexRankSummarizer
from sumy.summarizers.text_rank import TextRankSummarizer
In [82]:
htmlpass=HtmlParser.from_url(url, Tokenizer('english'))
summarizer=LsaSummarizer()
summarizer = LsaSummarizer(Stemmer('english'))
summarizer.stop_words = get_stop_words('english')
summary=summarizer(htmlpass.document,10)
print(summary)

(<Sentence: The term "world war" is used by Karl Marx and his associate, Friedrich Engels , [1] in a series of articles published around 1850 called The Class Struggles in France .>, <Sentence: In English, the term "First World War" had been used by Charles  Court Repington , as a title for his memoirs (published in 1920); he had noted his discussion on the matter with a Major Johnstone of Harvard University in his diary entry of September 10, 1918.>, <Sentence: Speculative fiction authors had been noting the concept of a Second World War in 1919 and 1920, when Milo Hastings wrote his dystopian novel, City of Endless Night .>, <Sentence: Due to this fact, a very minute conflict between two countries had the potential to set off a domino effect of alliances, triggering a world war.>, <Sentence: The fact that the powers involved had large overseas empires virtually guaranteed that such a war would be worldwide, as the colonies' resources would be a crucial strategic factor.>, <Sentence: The United States , the Soviet Union , and Canada deported and interned minority groups within their own borders, and largely because of the conflict, many ethnic Germans were later expelled from Eastern Europe .>, <Sentence: The old European empires either collapsed or were dismantled as a direct result of the wars' crushing costs and, in some cases, their fall was due to the defeat of imperial powers.>, <Sentence: The United States became firmly established as the dominant global superpower, along with its ideological foe, the Soviet Union, in close competition.>, <Sentence: World War II began last week at 5:20 a. m. (Polish time) Friday, September 1, when a German bombing plane dropped a projectile on Puck, fishing village and air base in the armpit of the Hel Peninsula.>, <Sentence: CS1 maint: ASIN uses ISBN ( link ) Book regarding alleged WWIV ^ "World War IV: Let's call this conflict what it is" .>)

summarizer_3 = TextRankSummarizer()
summarizer_3 = TextRankSummarizer(Stemmer('english'))
summarizer_3.stop_words = get_stop_words('english')
summary_3 =summarizer_3(htmlpass.document,2)
for sentence in summary_3:
    print(sentence)
